text:
This is the best!  Being a Floridian, I have had my share of both very good and very bad Key Lime Pie.  I did make a few changes to the recipe after reading the reviews.  I only used 4 egg yolks, I used 2 cans sweetened condensed milk, and I used 1 cup key lime juice.  Hint**If you can not find any key lime juice then just use equal parts lemon and lime juice (best if fresh). These adjustments will make more filling than needed, but the texture and taste is better.  I had to increase my baking time by 15 minutes.  I prebaked my redi-crust and this came out great. The new #1 key lime pie for my family.

text:
This was so unbelievably easy to make & produced such a delicious key lime pie!  I first made it in August for my mother-in-law's visit & wasn't sure how the recipe was going to turn out.  But it came out wonderfully & my mother-in-law could not stop raving about it!  I had to print her a copy of this recipe before she left for the airport, & I have also emailed it to my sister-in-law upon her mom's request that she try this recipe.  It has the perfect amount of richness & tartness for us (a small sliver goes a long way).  The whipped cream topping was a beautiful touch!  I used a Keebler reduced fat graham cracker crust & altered the recipe according to another reviewer's suggestions.  I used 4 egg yolks, 2 (14 oz) cans of sweetened condensed milk, & 1 cup of bottled key lime juice.  i had to bake for 20-25 minutes instead of just 15 minutes.  We found out that it also tastes best when refrigerated for at least several hours.  Hope you enjoy this pie as much as my family & I did!

text:
As written, a four star recipe--with the modifications I made, five star. First, I thought this pie deserved a homemade graham cracker crust, which I baked first, then cooled. Thinking this would be a little too eggy with 5 yolks, I used only four--perfect. I also knew the custard could stand a little more tartness, so I added 1-1/2 tsp. of grated lime zest to the filling. Perfect.  I baked it at 350 degrees for 15 minutes, then when cooled, topped the pie with 1 cup of sweetened whipped cream. Light and refreshing citrus-y pie, and the perfect complement to a spicy Mexican meal.

text:
Great recipe!  It was a little more tart than I like, but that can be fixed by adjusting some of your measurements.  I use the following: 3/4 c. key lime juice (Nelly & Joe's brand), 2 cans sweetened condensed milk, and 4 egg yolks.  It comes out perfect EVERY time, and people constantly ask for the recipe.  Trust me... these measurements are the way to go.  I've made it this way probably 20 times at least!!!  You can also easily cut back on fat and calories by using lowfat sweetened condensed milk -- you will never know the difference.

text:
For those of you like me...born without common sense.  Thoroughly mix the condensed milk and the lime juice. IN A SEPARATE BOWL...beat the egg yolks until smooth. Take a tbsp of the condensed milk and mix it into the eggs. When combined add another couple spoonfulls to the eggs. Now that your egg mix is no longer bright yellow add it to the big bowl of milk and lime juice...This is what people mean by tempering. If you just dump it all into a bowl together...you get really creamy filling with scrambled egg bits. Lime and egg DO NOT MIX ALONE. The citric acid will "cook" the eggs. Other than that this is a really good recipe:)

text:
This pie is so divinely good! I used all 5 egg yolks, and about a can and a half of sweetened condensed milk. I also increased the amount of lime juice to about 2/3s of a cup - these proportions gave it the perfect amount of sweet-tart flavor for my tastes. I also added the zest of 3 key limes for extra flavor, and 2 small drops of green food coloring for a very light lime color. While I usually prefer whipped cream, I topped it with whipped topping, because that is what my boyfriend's family prefers, (I had cooked dinner for them.) and I think it works better with the rich filling than heavy cream would. Light cream would probably be just as good. Everyone loved this pie... its easy, quick, and delicious. What more could you want?

text:
I've tried different versions of this recipe, but most are non-bake and don't come out. This one came out perfect. Tangy with a smooth texture. If you prefer a lighter, less custardy texture, whip the egg whites and fold into the milk/egg/juice mixture. Then, bake for 30 minutes at 250 degrees (yes, 250). It will have a very mousse-like texture. I used this technique after reading another key lime pie recipe and taking the best of it and adding it to this recipe. I like both the original recipe here AND the lighter, mousse-like version. Wonderful fresh lime flavor in both.

text:
I have made this no less than 50 times and it is my most requested recipe!  I also use 4 yolks, 1 cup of lime juice (fresh, bottled...sometimes 1/2 lemon, 1/2 lime, you CAN'T go wrong) and 2 cans of sweetened condensed milk, regular or low fat.  For the crust I make my own and I think this is the "secret" that makes it a favorite.  I put one sleeve of graham crakers (= 1 cup when crushed), 3T sugar, 1t ground ginger and about 1/4 c of coconut, toasted or regular (both work well) in food processor.  Combine until graham crackers are fine.  If you want more coconut, throw a little more in, but leave as flakes, makes a nice texture for the crust.  Mix with 5T of melted butter, press into pie dish or springform and bake for 8-10 mins @ 375.  Okay, this may sound crazy, but I promise it works.  When I have made dinners for other families, but am rushed on time, I have made two regular crusts and divided the pie filling to make two pies.  It truly works!  Yes, the pies will be a little less "tall", but it is still great and for those watching their calories, you will have fewer, but still get to have dessert :)

text:
Yes, this is the one you want to make. Yes, that's why there's over 100 reviews for this 1 recipe - it's that good (+ easy)!
I love key lime pie and got my hands on some key lime juice (finally!). I had never made one myself before but this recipe is great - easy, idiot proof, and tastes great. Everyone loved it and the pie was totally finished.
I used a vanilla-wafer crust instead of a graham-cracker one. I thought that flavor crust would work better (vanilla-lime-cream flavors all in 1 pie).  Just for prosperity here's my crust: 30 vanilla wafer cookies, 1/3 cup brown sugar, 2-3 tablespoons of butter. In food processer, blend cookes to small crumbs then add sugar + butter. Press into greased pie pan. Add key-lime-pie mix + bake. Anyhow - Loved this recipe. THANKS!

text:
I don't understand why everyone's trying to change this recipe... if done right, it's good like it is. I made this recipe with the ingredients as written, and it came out great (only I added 3 drops of green food coloring) I used 1/2 c. Nellie and Joe's Key West Lime Juice, 1 can sweetened condensed milk, and 5 egg yolks. For the crust, I used Keebler Shortbread crust instead of graham (I like it better, it tastes like butter cookies). I tempered the eggs, meaning I mixed the juice and condensed milk together in one bowl, beat the egg yolks in a seperate bowl, and gradually mixed the milk mixture, one tbs. at a time, into the egg mixture. I think the custard comes better like this, it comes out a weird texture if you just dump it all into a bowl and mix at once, because the eggs and citric acid in the lime juice don't really jive well. Must be combined slowly. That's the key. I baked at 350 degrees for 20 minutes. Chilled overnight. Came out perfect, smooth and creamy, not eggy at all, bursting with flavor, not too strong, not too tangy, not too sweet,  just right.. needs no alterations at all. This ones a keeper. Thank you Dinner2 for a great recipe!

For those who can't find key lime juice, it's almost always in the mixed-drink section of the alcohol aisle in your grocery store (if you live in a state where you can purchase alcohol in a grocery store).  It's by the margarita salts, grenadine, martini accessories, bottle openers... usually the brand is "Nellie & Joe's Key West Lime Juice."  By the way, this is a great pie recipe.  I did it with 4 yolks, 2 cans condensed milk, and 1 cup key lime juice.

text:
The first time I made this I accidentally put four WHOLE eggs in. I was really worried it wouldn't taste good but it still turned out delicious! Oh, and I also used regular lime juice instead of key limes. So then I was curious how much difference there really was in flavor and texture if I were to do it the correct way. So I made two pies at the same time- one with 4 egg yolks and 1/2 cup of key lime juice squeezed directly from about 20 little key limes (very time consuming-ha!) and the other pie I used two whole eggs (as suggested by other reviews when substituting for just yolks) and regular lime juice. the latter turned out just as good as my original (I think whether you use 2 eggs or 4 it's still good) and with a mild lime taste...and the actual key lime pie made just with yolks.....was AMAZING!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! I didn't think there could be that much of a difference but there really is! It was 100 % better than the other one in my opinion. Much more tart and bursting with flavor. I guess the regular lime pie would be better for someone who likes more mild flavoring. But there you go. That's the difference and it is a BIG one.

I made my own homemade graham cracker crust and I added two teaspoons of grated lime zest. 350* for ten minutes was just right. This is almost a five, but I think it needs the lime zest to give it that extra oomph. My kids and I especially liked this. NOTE: For those who thought this was really tart, my advice is to make this quite a few hours before you want to serve it. The longer it sets, in my opinion, the better it gets. It mellows and really gets good. If you can get it to last that long, that is. ;)

Simply delicious. Being a resident of Savannah, GA, this tastes very authentic. If you use a premade graham cracker crust though, I'd add 50% more sweetened condensed milk. If you want a true, Southern key lime pie, DO NOT ADD GREEN FOOD COLORING. True Key Lime Pie is a whitish shade, not green at all. This is as good as any from fine Southern restaurants: tart and custardy. Enjoy!

text:
Wonderful, classic dessert, inspiring comments from this seasoned lemon and lime meringue pie baker:  I hope "prepared"  doesn't mean the graham cracker pie crust already in the pan, purchased from the store, ready to bake. Nabisco's original graham crackers have reappeared on grocery shelves after several years' absence and are easy to transform into a crust. Small crumbs are a snap when using rolling pin  to smash and roll over the crackers while still in their waxed wrappings. To the crushed graham crackers, add just a little melted butter and sugar, to taste -- not much is needed, just enough to hold crumbs together in the pan. Spread moistened crumbs around the pan and press another pan the same or smaller size onto the crumbs for even thickness, but this step isn't necessary.   The crust, if it makes it to the oven (try not to  eat the crust right out of the pan before it's baked) is truly worth the tiny bit of extra effort. You won't go back to store-bought.This recipe is similar, but simpler, than the classic lemon meringue pie recipe found on the condensed milk can label, which I've been using since I was 11. But for those who love the sourness of lemon or lime meringue pies, finely grate some lime peel and perhaps also touch of lemon peel and a tiny bit of lemon extract to the lime pie.

text:
I've never made key-lime pie before but this one was so easy and came out great!  It almost tasted like The Cheesecake Factory's Key Lime Cheese Cake.  I put a dollop of whipped cream on top and my guest and fiance loved it!  I followed the reviewers recipes and used two cans of condensed milk.  I couldn't find key lime juice so I squeezed 5 fresh lemons, 7 fresh limes, and 5 key limes (the little limes) which was exactly one cup of juice, and used that instead.    I did make my own crust.  It is an awesome crust and so simple.  Its the same crust I use on my cheesecake.  Buy cinnamon honey graham crackers and crush up two of the packages that come inside the box (not two boxes) into crumbs.  Add 2/3 cup white sugar and 1 cup melted butter.  Stir it well.  You should be able to press this into a pie or cheesecake pan.  Make sure if you use a cheesecake pan you put another pan under it in the oven to catch any dripping butter.

text:
Great recipe.  Made it the first time and thought I would "improve" on it by adding a little lime zest.  Big mistake, very bitter.  Who knew that you aren't supposed to zest key limes?  Made it the second time and stuck to the recipe.  Duh?  Perfect.  A couple of comments . . . key lime pie is not green.  Unless you add red food coloring to your apple pie, don't add green to key lime.  Second, the room in the pie shell is for the topping, traditionally meringue and in this recipe whipped cream or whipped topping.  If you didn't have a topping, it would be extremely tart.  This recipe is "easy" because it uses a prepared crust and doesn't require "fresh" lime juice, not because it has only three ingredients.  "Authentic" key lime pie filling is made of egg yolks (the whites are used for the meringue), sweetened condensed milk, and lime juice.  I have used fresh juice--that takes care of quick--and it takes about 16-18 key limes for 1/2 cup juice.  I have also made this once using fat-free condensed milk and 3/4 cup Egg Beaters.  It worked great.  Thanks, Pat.

The recipe for Key Lime Pie on the label is almost identical, except uses only 3 egg yolks and bakes at 350,  Food for thought.

text:
Very good and easy.  I have made key lime pie before, but sometimes it would be runny so I wanted to try this version (the other recipe I made before was the same except for not baked at all).   I read on another review that you should mix the yolks and condensed milk, well, but then add the lime juice just until blended- overmixing can prevent the pie from setting up.  I baked it as directed and it turned out perfect.  As for some complaints that it was not alot of filling, this is how I have always had it.  It is such a dense pie in that you don't need alot of filling, especially when topped with freshly sweetened whipped cream.  Next time I will whip the left over egg whites with a little sugar, and top the pie with that instead of the whipped cream.  I have had it like that before and that is good also.

text:
I've made this twice now....sooo yummy! My hubby loves it, and he's the key lime pie expert! Thanks for sharing such an easy recipe! I'm not sure now where I read this, but I've been taking the advice of a fellow reader to juice the limes in a garlic press. With some of the smaller limes, I just cut them in half so they can fit. If they are larger, I quarter them. It makes juicing them so easy...just make sure you point the juicer way down in a large bowl or it will squirt everywhere! Thanks again for a "real" tasting key lime pie!

This is for those of you who add food coloring (or other color) to this: When we honeymooned in Key West, our tour guide told us, "Key limes produce pale yellow juice. Key lime pie should be pale yellow, too. If you ever order Key Lime Pie and it's green, send it back and get something chocolate!" Something to think about as you make "authentic" Key Lime Pie! Regardless of color, I know you'll enjoy this yummy pie!!!

text:
WAY BETTER THAN STORE-BOUGHT!!!! This pie was absolutely delicious!!! With the review suggestions (4 egg yolks, 2 cans milk, 1 cup lime juice. bake @ 350 for 20-25 min) it came out PERFECT!!! I LOVE key lime pie but this was my first time trying to make it at home. I will never ever buy it in the stores again. It does come out tart (which I happen to like) so if you want it with less kick, cut back on the lime juice. I did notice that the filling was more yellow than green when I was mixing it so I added some lemon-lime kool-aid to it to get that true lime green color. This also added a little extra punch that I dont think I would have gotten with food coloring. You can kind of tweak the amount you add to your own taste and color preference. I used about 1/3 of a pack- and then used the leftover to make kool-aid with while the pie was baking!!! If you mix the lime juice, milk, and kool-aid together first you can taste and alter it before you add the eggs without worrying about eating the raw yolks. I did not add any whip cream on top until I cut and served it (If you let it sit on the pie in the fridge it will run and be a soggy mess, especially if it is store bought and not homemade whip cream) I also kept mine in the freezer instead of the fridge so that the pie would be firm (and not quite so mushy) Anyway this was incredible and ridiculously easy to make!! TRY IT!!!

SUPER easy and delicious! I couldn't find key lime juice and didn't feel like sqeezing a bunch of them either so used half lemon, half lime juice that come in the little plastic fruit shapped containers and it was still fantastic. This is literally the easiest pie you will ever make. I forgot that most reviewers said to use 4 yolks instead of 5 and I used 5 - don't know what difference 1 less egg yolk would have made or that this pie could have been any better without it. I used a store bought shortbread ready-made crust and it came out just fine. The filling was so smooth, set up beautifully and tasted amazing. I will definitely make this pie again and again. The one thing I did remember to do was double the recipe. Good thing too because a single batch wouln't have filled the pie shell nearly enough. Make and enjoy!!

Fantastic. Easy. I used the recomendations from other users. On top of that,  I made my own meringue topping: (Use stand up mixer or very strong hand mixer,  high power!) beat the 4 egg whites until frothy. Gradually add 1 cup sugar, beat until stiff peaks form. I cooked the key lime pie for 15 minutes, took it out to spoon the meringue on top, and returned into oven immediately, baking the pie for the remaining 10-15 minutes.

text:
After reading the many positive reviews of this pie I gave it a try.  I wanted to find a style of key lime filling that was more dense/solid.  Even though this pie is more custard-like it was absolutely terrific and easily matches the very best key lime pies I've ever tasted...and I LOVE key lime pie.  Its level of tartness is perfect for my tastes.

The preparation was very simple.  I followed the directions to a tee, (I used key lime juice from a bottle), but I would have added two directions that may seem obvious to most...1) make sure to allow the pie to cool completely on a wire rack and THEN 2) cool the pie in the refrigerator for 2 to 3 hours.  I would also think about drizzling a little rasberry sauce for occasional dipping and using a high quality whipped cream.

Enjoy!

This could not have been easier and is the best key lime pie I've ever had. I made it for my mom's birthday (she's a major key lime pie fan) and she loved it so much that I've since made it many many times over. It's a big hit! 

We used Nellie & Joes Key Lime Juice (don't just use lime juice, it's important to get real key lime juice) and a pre-made Keebler graham cracker crust. The finished pie was sweet with a wonderful tart lime flavor. It has a great natural color (a very pretty light pale green). Once it has cooled, I add whipped cream on top to balance out the tartness. If you bring this to a party I guarantee everyone will be begging for the recipe.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Definately throw in the zest from the limes-4 teaspoons is good- the oven releases it's flavor and the result is a more intensely flavored, and prettier green pie (rather than yellowish). Whisk  it into the yolks(4 is plenty), then add the rest of the ingredients and let sit at room temperature for 30 minutes, which helps the filling begin to thicken before it is even placed in the oven. This is because the lime juice causes the proteins in the yolks and milk to bond together. Definitely try this if you are having problems with a loose or soupy filling, rather than overcooking. Then proceed with the recipe. I have found that if you can't find fresh key limes, Persian limes give a much better taste than bottled juice- citrus flavor diminishes soon after being squeezed and can turn harsh-no matter what kind of citrus juice it is, there is no comparison between bottled and fresh. Add a touch of lemon if you want. Also-a homemade crust is soooo much better than store bought ones, which are made with shortening rather than butter.  After baking the crust a bit, I cook my pie at 325 degrees for 15 minutes. Next time I am going to try a coconut graham cracker crust: 4 tablespoons unsweetened shredded and toasted coconut, 9 whole graham crackers, 2 tablespoons sugar, and 5 tablespoons melted butter. Grind the crackers, coconut, and sugar in the food processor, then poor the melted butter through the feed tube and process, scraping down. Bake 325, 15 min, let cool.

text:
This pie is superb! I don't know if any of you have heard of the Historic Jekyll Island Hotel, but I live near it and one of the restaurants there serves almost exactly this same pie! There is one less egg yolk and one less T. of lime juice, but it's almost the same recipe. I recommend making whipped cream topping like they do: 2 cups heavy whipping cream, 3 T. sugar and 1 tsp of vanilla extract blended together and spread on top of the pie to really compliment this delicious recipe! I also make my own graham cracker crust to really set this pie off to another level! Combine 1.5 cups graham cracker crumbs, 1/2 cup sugar and 5 T. melted butter. Bake at 350 for seven minutes and let cool before filling with lime mixture. YUM!!

text:
This was my first time to make a key lime pie. It's my boyfriend's favorite dessert, and I decided to make it for his birthday.  I put 7 egg yolks, 3/4 cup lime juice and 1 1/2 cans of condensed milk for more filling. I also put 1.5-2.0 ounces of lime jello mix for consistency and color. It turned out beautifully. Everyone loved it. Eggs make this pie a bit custardy, and the jello mix made look naturally green(not the fake food coloring look). I topped it with canned whipped cream and lime zest. Definitely recommended.

text:
This was an easy recipe.  I bought a bag of key limes because they were cute and decided to make the pie.  I prepared the boxed pie crust mix and baked the crust according to the directions putting parchment paper on the crust and filling it with dried beans.  After 10 min. I removed the paper and beans and baked it for 5 minutes more.  While waiting for the crust to bake and cool, I squeezed all the limes and prepared the filling.  I thought the final product was quite tasty but a smidgen too tart for me.  Next time I will add maybe a tablespoon of sugar and/or sprinkle sugar on the filling before I put it in the oven to bake. Thanks for an easy recipe.

text:
I love this recipe! I have baked it many times I'm in Florida though I've tried other self proclaimed "best key lime pies" they didn't quite suffy my own palate until I baked my own. I have created/followed a few different modifications: Definitely cut back on egg yolks -5 makes it too eggy and hard-
I substituted the two cans of CM for 1 fat free CM 1/2 can of evaporated milk 4 egg yolks pure vanilla lime zest (about 2 spoons) and depending on how tart limey and sour you want it 1/3 to 1 cup of key lime juice (I've use reg. fresh lime juice about 1/3 and lots of finely zest) it's so creamy so good! 
**Tip: mix all ingredients but the juice take your time as the custard will thick out while adding the juice then putting in oven @ 375 for 20min then set for an hr or two. I use a homemade Graham crust yummy!!

text:
I really improvised on this pie, combining two recipes, as I couldn't decide which sounded the best.  One recipe for white chocolate key lime pie had white chocolate and cream added to the Eagle Brand milk and lime juice.  And this recipe with the egg yolks sounded good, so I just added the white chocolate chips (1 cup) and cream (1/2 cup) to this recipe and added another 2 egg yolks--I know, that's a lot  of egg yolks, but I wanted to make sure it set up with the added ingredients.  I also used about 1 1/4 cups lime juice.  I baked it for about 30 minutes, too.  It did set up just fine and tasted really good, but the white chocolate flavor wasn't noticeable, so don't think I'd do that again.  Probably would just stick to this recipe as posted.

text:
I've been looking for ways to utilize the key limes from my tree and this recipe caught me as one simple to make. I followed some of the suggestions in the previous comments. I used 4 egg yolks and 2 14 oz cans of sweetened condensed milk per pie, but only used 1/2 cup of lime juice. I made two pies and cooked them at 350 for 20 minutes. I then let the cool in the refrigerator. One I pulled out the next evening for a potluck, the next stayed in the fridge for 2 extra days. The first one was very tart and my wife complained about it. The second was very smooth with a wonderful full lime flavor, but was not the least bit sour. I took it to work and my coworkers kept coming back for seconds. Definitely a winner in my book.

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was super tasty and impressive!  Used 4 egg yolks, one cup key lime juice, 2 cans of condensed milk and store bought graham cracker crust.  For the key limes: I found a bag of key limes (tiny!) at my local grocery store (in Massachusetts at Shaws) -- was time consuming to juice them almost all of them (with a juicer) and didn't even get a full cup (I don't think all would have made a full cup - and/or would just barely)...glad I bought a backup bottle. Also put some lime zest in the mix - maybe one tsp. This is sweet - but tasty - I liked the extra tartness from the zest.  My bake time was about 25 minutes - watch it from 15 to 20 minutes...it just started to look like it was about to get golden (that would be too far!)...clearly done. Chilled in the fridge for about 2-3 hours.  Reserved a few limes for garnish: I sliced and candied 2 of them (made about 10 slices)..basically sliced thin, blanched for 2 minutes in boiling water, pulled out. Refilled pan with one C water, one C sugar, brought to a gentle boil and put the slices back in, simmered for about 25-30 minutes. Took out limes and "dried" on a baking rack for about 1 hour, then tossed in a bowl with a little sugar to coat. Arranged on top -- Impressive and got props!  Finished with store bought whipped cream...which makes it fancier looking around the edges -- and grated lime zest on it (like the pic!) Just put it on right before serving...it wilts a bit.  This pie will make you a superstar - tastes amazing, easy

text:
Pretty good pie!  Lovely flavor!  I used others suggestions: 4 yolks and 2 cans sweetened cond. milk (I used the fat free kind).  I also used a pre-baked pie crust and key lime juice from the bottle.  I baked it for 30 minutes since I had an additional can of milk.  My dad loved this pie!  My only mistake was that after it was well chilled, I topped it with whipped cream from the can -HORRIBLE, HORRIBLE MISTAKE!!  The whipped cream deflated and liquified and is now seeping down the sides of the crust, I'm sure making it soggy as I type.  We ate some to still enjoy the flakiness of the crust but I'm afraid that experience is over.  In the future I will definitely use heavy whipping cream to make my own whipped cream -it stays firm and pretty and doesn't ruin your pie!  Don't make my mistake.

text:
I followed the 4 eggs, 2 cans condensed milk and 1 cup key lime juice suggestions and ended up with enough filling for two crusts! Perhaps I made it too fluffy? I took the time to first beat the egg yolks for about 4 minutes and then slowly added the condensed milk while still beating on a medium speed. I finally slowed my mixer to 'stir' and added the key lime juice.

While the first pie was baking, I sent my boyfriend out to get a second crust and I added some more key lime juice to the second half of the batter (about a tablespoon) and some lime zest. This second one came out much more tart than the first and I think was preferred by most of my coworkers. However, both pies were pretty much devoured and got rave reviews!!

Next time, I'm going to try to half the modified recipe as I don't need two pies and modify it a little. I like the more tart version of the pie except that it didn't hold together as well. I think there wasn't enough eggs in it. SO I'm going to try 3 eggs, 1 can condensed milk and 1/2 cup and 1 tbsp of key lime juice. I love experimenting!

text:
Everyone was bugging me to make Irresistible Pecan Pie again (look it up and try it!), but no, I'd noticed we had a lot of limes in the fruit and vegetable fridge drawer and wanted to try something different. I don't know if these are the same as 'key limes,' they were just regular old New Zealand limes that my mother had been putting slices of in her gin and tonic. Important note for non-American cooks saying 'What on earth is a graham cracker crust?' Graham crackers are essentially the same as plain wheat digestive biscuits. I used these in the 'Graham Cracker Crust III' recipe and it turned out perfectly (okay, the edges burned a little bit because I set the oven timer wrong, but I cut those off and it tasted fine). Malt biscuits would also work well. Although a lot of reviews here complained that there was too little filling for a nine-inch pie dish, I didn't find this a problem, although my pie was not full to the brim. I think a nice way to top it up might be to cover the filling (after it's baked and cooled) with an arrangement of kiwi fruit slices (hairy skins removed!) - the colours and flavours would complement each other. I added a couple of drops of green food colouring because the original mixture was a distinct yellow colour - from the egg yolks, I guess. It looked more lemony than lime so I thought I'd help it along. And the final verdict? Everyone really enjoyed it, and I think in future they'll bug me to make key lime pie as well!

text:
This is the recipe passed down through 5 generations of my family from Florida and I have passed it to generations 6 and 7.  You only need 4 egg yolks, not 5 and the rest of it is correct. You can bake it or not, up to you and how you feel about raw egg yolks.  If you are going to bake it, 15 minutes at 350 and chill till serving.  If you are NOT going to bake it, after mixing, let it sit in the fridge for 8 hours to "chemically" cook it and it will set up.  The unbaked version yields a softer creamier texture but both are good, it's just personal preference.  I've been making this pie for 56 years, it never fails.

text:
I am a native Floridian and have been making and eating Key Lime Pie for literally decades.  I have eaten some that was divine, and some that was an abomination. 

This recipe is as close to mine as I can find (and of course I like mine best :)).  The only differences are that I bump up the  amount of condensed milk to about 19 ounces and the amount of key lime juice to six ounces, and I use four eggs.  I have made this pie too many times to count and it has earned some of the best compliments I have ever received.

Two pro-tips.  (1) If you can, squeeze your own fresh key limes.  It will be fresher and better than any store-bought juice.  A single one pound bag (about 20 limes) yields the perfect amount of juice for one pie.  If you can't find key limes at your grocer, then use the bottled Key West lime juice rather than Persian limes which are not tart enough.  (2)  Make your own graham cracker crust using a recipe you can find here.  Quick and easy and soooooooo much better than premade pie shells.

Last note.  This filling is dense.  It is supposed to be dense.  That is how true Key Lime pie is.  There is another type of pie that folks call Key Lime Pie that uses egg whites, often substitutes Persian limes, adds green food coloring (!), and whips it all up into a light, whipped, filling.  It is not a bad pie if done correctly (and preferably with a pastry dough crust rather than a graham crust), and some restaurants even in Florida serve it.  But I wish folks would just c

The easiest and best tasting pie I ever made. I am a novice when it comes to pies. I used as directed 1/2 cup of lime juice, 5 yolks & 1 can of sweetened condensed milk. I used a food processor to mix ingredients throughly and it helped with making the filling very light in consistence (if I had s hand mixer I would have used that).. I used fresh squeezed key lime juice. I did add a touch of finely graded key lime rind to the filling. I baked the pie about 6 minutes longer until I saw the filling rise and firm up a bit. I followed the advice of another reviewer but putting the pie the the freezer for 30 minutes the the fridge from 30 minutes but I cooled it for about 15 minutes before putting it the freezer. I had great reviews and will make this again.

text:
I'm in college and so having my guy friends wait 4 hours for a pie is just not an option. This pie is fast and disappeared almost instantly. However,  I NEVER use a pre-made pie crust from the store, I defiantly recommend making your own using 1 1/2 cups cinnamon gram crackers, 6 tablespoons melted butter, and 1/3 cup sugar. Mix it and mold it to a pie dish. Stick it in the oven for 7 mins at 375. You can make the pie mix while it cools. It is also worth it because you don't have to change the recipe size for the pie filling, it fits the tin perfectly! Making your own crust does take a bit longer, but its totally worth it! I also chill this pie for about an hr. On hot days its much better to have a cool slice of key lime than a warm one. Amazing pie! Add extra thick whipped cream and its the bee's knees!

I am giving this recipe only four out of five stars because I, like so many other reviewers, modified it to a large extent.  I used four egg yolks, two cans of condensed milk, the juice of one lemon in addition to one cup of (Persian/supermarket) lime juice, and a large portion (about a tablespoon) of lime zest.  Oh...and I baked my pie (in a springform pan) for about twenty-five or thirty minutes.  All that being said ... it was great.  Nice texture and nicely tart/sweet.  I had never made a KeyLime pie before, but my friend who is a big fan of the genre said it was very good.  I will enthusiastically make again (with my modifications).  Thanks!  (And thanks to all who reviewed and suggested changes!)

This pie was so easy it almost felt like there was no way it could be good, but it was!  I followed the suggestions of others and used two cans of condensed milk, one cup of key lime juice, and four egg yolks.  It filled the pie crust perfectly.  I added some green food coloring and got a very pretty pale green color.  It set perfectly when baked for 20 minutes.  I served it with a dollop of canned whipped cream...  next time I may make some fresh whipped cream and top the whole pie with it.  It was tart and sweet and, as far as I know, that is how key lime pie is supposed to be!

text:
I am by far not an experienced cook. I am, however, a lover of Key Lime pie.  I found this recipe and decided to give it a shot. I read a few of the reviews and made it using the following:  Two 14oz cans of fat free condensed milk, 10" pre-made graham cracker crust, RealLime juice. I messed up and used the egg white instead of the yolk (told you I am not a cook), but surprisingly it still turned out okay.  I baked it for 25 minutes like the reviewers said and it came out perfect. I chilled it overnight and had a piece for breakfast. DELICIOUS! I was a little "puffy" (which I think may have happened because of using the egg white instead of the yolk) but it was still wonderful.  I will definitely make another one ... this time using the yolk like it says. I am also going to try to add just a little more lime juice, as I really like my pies very tart.  All in all this is a keeper. I will be tweaking it just to see if I can get it as tart as I like ... but that is all.  Thanks to all who have contributed to the adjustments. It is great.

Excellent! I used 4 yolks and 2 cans of SCM and increased the lime juice to even more than a cup. (1 1/3 or so!). Everyone loved the tart taste. Cool the crust for 20 minutes or so in the pie pan but on a cooling rack before adding the pie filling. Homemade whipped cream and the crowd went wild.

text:
If you're looking for a light, fluffy pie, look elsewhere.  There seem to be a lot of differing preferences when it comes to texture, and for those who want a creamy filling, this is the pie for you.  I used about 2/3C lime juice and the zest of half of my key limes, and then baked it about 5 minutes extra, and this still wasn't quite tart enough for me, but the flavor was out of this world.  The recipe I'm looking for has a bit lighter texture than this one does though, so although this was wonderful for a creamy dessert, I'm going to give Key Lime Pie  I a try, and see if that's a bit closer to what I had in mind.  

All in all, this makes for an amazing, creamy pie.

text:
My first pie and it was DELICIOUS. I'm so proud of how perfectly this came out. Just the right balance of tartness and sweetness. I served with fresh, unsweetened whipped cream.

A tip for squeezing those tiny limes: I used my 1950s kitchen appliance the "Juice-O-Mat". It's a press juicer and it took no time to get a 1/2 cup. You can get these old juicers at a vintage shop where they sell kitchen stuff. These things were built to last and are better quality than the ones today, and it's non-electric. There are tons out there and they aren't expensive(I know, I'm a dealer).

Delicious!  A hit with everyone. I live in Uzbekistan, so I had to make some changes based on availability of ingredients.  

I used lemons instead of limes, as no limes are available here in the winter.  I juiced them in an electric juicer, and then added about 2 teaspoons of lemon rind to the mix to increase flavor and tartness.

In any case, this is a delicious recipe and really easy to make.

My husband and I just returned from Key West, and this was as good as the pie we ate when we were there. I would definitely make this one again.

text:
Since this was my first attempt at a Key Lime Pie, I did not change the recipe except to add green food coloring.
Like the other reviews warned, this did not fill my 9" pie crust, but I just made a quick meringue with the egg whites, cream of tartar and Sweet & Low (was out of sugar) & it turned out fine.  I didn't bake it as long (about 8 minutes less) because the meringue was getting too brown, but after letting it set in the fridge overnight the consistancy was great and the flavor was wonderful!  I didn't think it was to tart...the sweetness of the graham cracker crust really balanced it out.  Thanks for such a great recipe.

This is a wonderfully simple and delicious recipe! My family loves it at holidays. It deserves five stars exactly as it is. Its all just preference, people! So the great part is that after you make it once, its easy to tweak if you like it a little more tart or a little more sweet. Note that if you end up using a pre-bought graham cracker crust, this recipe isnt quite enough filling,  so you will need to make more (I use additional sweetened condensed milk and lime juice, and stuck with the four egg yolks). Delicious!

This pie is WAY too heavy and WAY too sweet.

text:
This is so far, my favorite version of a key lime pie; however, I only it a 4-star rating because there are some adjustments I make that I think make it a 5-star pie. 
Firstpersonal preference, of courseI use traditional (homemade) pie crust instead of graham cracker crust. 

I also zest the limes and add about 1 1/4 tsp zest to the filling and set 1/2 tsp aside for topping.

And when I juice the limes, I add maybe a tsp or so of the lime pulp to the filling as well. 
And I increase the lime juice amount slightly, using somewhere between 1/2 c and 3/4 c.

Once its baked and cooled, I smear whipped cream (freshly made, not pre-made) across the whole pie and sprinkle the left over zest on top. 

Its delicious!

text:
If you're looking for simplicity, this is about as simple as you can get without doing the cringe-worthy powdered mix. It should be noted... If you want a finished pie, you should probably bake it for 20-30 minutes depending on your oven. Just watch the pie. Once you start seeing bubbles break the surface, it's ready to come out (the edges should be a slightly darker color than the center). Take it out and let it cool on top of the oven/stove, since it'd still be "cooking" for 5-10 minutes after you take it out.

I changed up the recipe ever so slightly by adding 2/3rd cup of key lime juice. With 1/2 cup it wouldn't have been properly tart. People really underestimate the power of condensed milk when it comes to adding juices. I was able to make 4 pies and top them with whipped cream (they were fine without it, but eh, aesthetics), all for 16 dollars. It was easy to make too, with the worst part being the egg separation for obvious messy reasons.

text:
Please READ! This recipe is only meh, unless you use FRESH squeezed lime juice and include the zest of the limes! Using bottled lime juice will yield a pie that tastes like floor cleaner. 
Ive made this same pie several times every summer for at least a decade, and everybody loves it. If you want to make it really exceptionally delicious do the following:
- Make your own graham cracker crust (1.5 cups of graham crackers, ground fine, six tablespoons melted butter, 1/4 cup sugar, baked at 375 for 8 minutes and cooled).
- Use fresh limes and their zest (4-6 limes yield a half cup)
-  combine the filling ingredients in a BLENDER. This way the zest gets ground up very fine and the condensed milk, egg yolks and juice are emulsified so that the filling is smooth and slightly aerated.
- Do Not Over Bake. Should still have some jiggle in the middle
- Top with lightly sweetened FRESH whipped cream. NOT cool whip. Yuck.

I took the advise of Shrae1 and it turned out amazing, Thank you!!!

This is the best! Being a Floridian, I have had my share of both very good and very bad Key Lime Pie. I did make a few changes to the recipe after reading the reviews. I only used 4 egg yolks, I used 2 cans sweetened condensed milk, and I used 1 cup key lime juice. Hint**If you can not find any key lime juice then just use equal parts lemon and lime juice (best if fresh). These adjustments will make more filling than needed, but the texture and taste is better. I had to increase my baking time by 15 minutes. I prebaked my redi-crust and this came out great. The new #1 key lime pie for my family.

text:
This is my FAVORITE Key Lime Pie recipe. My friend who owns Rock 'n Java in Cozumel gave me the ingredients she uses in her KLPs for the restaurant and I found this one to use for the ratios. EVERYBODY loves it. I've used a hand mixer and I've used a Vitamix. I've made it so many times that I don't know what I might have done differently each time but I've had it come out fluffyish and I've had it come out custardy which I've been told traditional KLPs are supposed to be. They were ALL very much enjoyed so I have ZERO complaints. If you want a light creamy pie, I suggest you find a recipe that calls for whipped cream or sour cream or egg whites. Oh, I make the crust with almond flour instead for a gluten free alternative, when my nut allergic son is not partaking, I add a few coarsely chopped pecans to crust and er'body goes NUTS for it. -pun intended :) Unfortunately, I have not found a keto recipe that I like, so for now, I just stick to cheesecake for a low-carb dessert. Enjoy!!!

text:
The only reason I'm giving this recipe 4 stars instead of 5 is because I'm a bit skeptical of the quantity of custard it makes. I've made this pie twice- the flavor is amazing, the texture is wonderful, but I find it hard to believe that the recipe makes enough custard for a 9 inch pie pan. I've had to double it each time- once with a pre-made Keebler crust and once with a homemade crust in a standard 9 inch glass pie plate. Both times, the recipe as stated barely filled half the pie shell. Doubling it is no hardship- it's a fantastic pie and deeper slices mean more yumminess!  Just double the baking time to 30 min and watch it closely for browning (which is a no-no). Also, someone suggested using a garlic press to squeeze the teeny key limes, and it works like a charm!!

text:
I saw a review here which mentioned that this pie came out like a very dense cheesecake when they tried it, and I'm afraid I had the same problem.  The flavor is good, but the texture is not what I'd wanted at all.  I used the user adaptation that calls for 4 egg yolks, 2 cans sweetened condensed milk, 1 cup lime juice, and baking it for 'twice as long' (I did exactly 30 min) at the exact temperature suggested.  This was the first key lime pie I've made, and the recipe doesn't tell you how full to fill the crust, so I had to guess, and filled it to about 1 cm below the top.  When I took it out of the oven, the edges of the filling were slightly brown, and the middle was very elevated, jiggly, and far less cooked than the outsides.  The texture is not silky smooth like every other key lime pie I've tried all my life, so as a native Floridian I was disappointed. After looking around some websites, it sounds like some people prefer this thicker texture, but I didn't realize key lime pie even comes this way so I'm going to try a different recipe next time, perhaps even a no-bake one if it's the eggs that made the texture bad in this one.

text:
I made this using regular limes, 4 eggs--as recommended by many users--and with adding zest. I also added the meringue topping from Lemon Meringue Pie III and the Shortbread Crust form this site. I had to bake the cake, though, for an extra 15 minutes and then left it in the oven (B/c I had to run out and frankly forgot to take it out). But even though it was still kind of warm and runny when we got home, it was still REALLY good. I made a tin foil tent over the cake for the last 15 minutes so the meringue wouldn't brown any more than it had already in the first 15 minutes. I will def. make this again. Next time, I'll bake for the first 15 min. without the meringue and then take it out, apply the meringue, and then put it back in for another 15 minutes.

text:
I used Shrae1's alterations to this recipe, and I think it's the first time that I've ever licked the spoon and bowl. (It was great baked too, don't get me wrong!) With the leftover filling, I filled a silicone muffin pan 6 x half. I'm not sure if it would work with a regular muffin pan, but I inverted and gently poked the bottom of each one to unmold them. Only the ones fully surrounded by crust made it out in one piece, so if you do this, make sure that your crust goes at least halfway up the sides of each cup!

...I have wanted to make this pie for a long time now and was actually waiting until I purchased Key Lime juice..never got around to it....SO...I followed the advice of SHRAE1 and used 1/2c ea lemon and lime juice.  Made my own crust (1c graham cc, 3Tbls sugar and 5Tbls melted butter & baked for 5 mins) and did not bother with the whipped topping. With these modifications mine took 20 mins to bake...my son and his friends had two pieces ea..very creamy!  Thanks Pat and SHRAE1. Will make this again when I get some real Key Lime juice.

text:
I did not change one thing about this recipe and it turned out GREAT!  I think it was the best key lime pie I ever had.  It had a good consistency and has a great flavor.  It is tart, but that's how I like my key lime pie.  It is really good with some whipped cream on top.  My grocery store (Dominicks) sells a bottle of key lime juice, so I used that.  The color of the pie is yellowish, but that is to be expected as that is the natural color of lime juice.  I suppose you could add food coloring to make it more green, but I prefer it with it's natural color!

This recipe was SO EASY and QUICK!  I would definitely recommend it!

text:
Oh so tasty! I did make the following suggested changes, however:
4 egg yolks
1 cup key lime juice
2 cans sweetened condensed milk
If think I would put more lime (about 3/4 cup to 1/4 cup lemon) juice, simply because I like the unique tang of the lime in my pie.  When mixing the milk in with everything else, it's like mixing milk into thick oatmeal, so make sure you mix it well.  Just a beaaautiful pie.

text:
Made the pie just the other day and it's all gone.  I couldn't find any key limes or key lime juice.  Instead I used fresh lime juice (approx. 4-5 avg. sized limes), plus 2 tsp. lime zest (looks great in the pie), 2 tsp white sugar, and 2-3 drops of green food coloring.  No more yellow pie and it's nice and tart. I also used "Graham Cracker Crust I" from this site for the crust. Easy and Outstanding, the way it should be.

I used this recipe as dessert for a dinner I did at our Elks Lodge.  The kids weren't as excited about the unique flavor of Key Lime as the adults -- but NO LEFTOVERS!  I was asked for the recipe by a number of people and that's always a good sign.  I used crusts from the Dollar Store (two for a buck!) and whipped topping from a can because it's pretty with less effort.  I used regular lime peels, sugared, for garnish.  Also, I live in Wyoming and I buy Key Lime Juice bottled at the local supermarket in my town of 7,000 -- ask for it since it's much easier than squeezing the little limes!
